  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_810be5a1-e9e2-4485-9cb7-c0f58cacd854'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2572089223" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2572089223" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2572089223?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060115456" href="/book/show/1052799.Old_Yeller">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2572089223" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14993667037744455993"><i>Old Yeller</i> is a coming of age story about a boy named Travis and his family living in Salt Lick, Texas in the 1860s. Travis is fourteen years old and yearns to be a man. His father is leaving for Abilene on a trip to drive cattle for money, and Travis will be left to man their home until his father returns.<br/><br/><i>“Now, Travis,” he said, “you’re getting to be a big boy; and while I’m gone, you’ll be the man of the family. I want you to act like one. You take care of Mama and Little Arliss. You look afte</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14993667037744455993" style="display:none"><i>Old Yeller</i> is a coming of age story about a boy named Travis and his family living in Salt Lick, Texas in the 1860s. Travis is fourteen years old and yearns to be a man. His father is leaving for Abilene on a trip to drive cattle for money, and Travis will be left to man their home until his father returns.<br /><br /><i>“Now, Travis,” he said, “you’re getting to be a big boy; and while I’m gone, you’ll be the man of the family. I want you to act like one. You take care of Mama and Little Arliss. You look after the work and don’t wait around for your mama to point out what needs to be done.”</i><br /><br />Even though Travis is now responsible for keeping his mother and younger brother Arliss safe, he’ll also have to keep up with chopping the wood and hunting for food. He feels pretty confident that he can take care of things while his father’s away and looks forward to getting his own horse when his father returns. Not long after, a stray yellow dog shows up and steals some of their meat. Travis is extremely furious about it and wants to hurt the dog, but little Arliss insists they keep him. Travis flat-out doesn’t want a dog again; he had a dog before that died and it was hard for him to get over. Little Arliss is persistent and wins him over. They name the dog Old Yeller.<br /><br /><i>“I guessed that when you are nearly a man, you have to learn to put up with a lot of aggravation from little old bitty kids.”</i><br /><br />Over time, Old Yeller doesn’t just keep Arliss entertained; he earns his keep and saves their lives multiple times. He’s a wonderful cow dog and great with the hogs too. Travis gets to where he depends on Old Yeller to help him around the land and grows to love him. Travis learns quickly that life on the frontier is often unpredictable and perilous. There are also many daily chores to maintain: keeping animals out of the corn patch, branding hogs, fetching water, hunting, and milking the cow. There’s also a disease known as hydrophobia going around and killing animals which is a big risk for humans too.<br /><br />I read this book when I was in elementary school and decided to read it with my children. I recall being emotional over the book when I was a child, but honestly this time around it wasn’t as sad. The ending is sort of revealed within the first pages which spares the reader in a way. I finally got teary in the end when Travis has a conversation with his dad about Old Yeller.<br /><br /><i>“That was as rough a thing as I ever heard tell of happening to a boy. And I’m mighty proud to learn how my boy stood up to it. You couldn’t ask any more of a grown man… It’s not a thing you can forget. I don’t guess it’s a thing you ought to forget. What I mean is, things like that happen. They may seem mighty cruel and unfair, but that’s how life is part of the time. But that isn’t the only way life is. A part of the time, it’s mighty good. And a man can’t afford to waste all the good part, worrying about the bad parts. That makes it all bad.”</i><br /><br />I enjoy Fred Gipson’s writing as it’s very graphic with detailed descriptions and imagery. You really get a sense of what life was like for this family with all their hard work and difficulties. It’s almost like you’re transported back to this time period on the frontier. It’s a great book to educate children about what life was like back then.<br /><br />We liked the characters in the book, especially Travis. With Travis as the narrator, you feel his emotions as he tells the story and you can see his character grow as he matures tremendously in the little time his father is gone. His mother is supportive and does a fine job caring for the family while their father is away. Little Arliss is a handful and he’s always getting into trouble. He bumps heads with Travis often, but Travis grows to understand him. Burn Sanderson is incredibly kind and respectful. I think the only character we found annoying was Bud Searcy and mainly because he was too chatty and lazy. He wasn’t willing to help, would quickly pass work onto someone else, and basically came around acting like he was there for support. What he really wants is just a free meal.<br /><br />Our hardcover edition is a previous library copy in really good shape. I’m unsure what year this edition is based on the copyright page. It’s definitely not a very old edition because it does list Fred Gipson’s last book and his death in 1973 on the back cover. I believe the first edition publisher was Harper &amp; Brothers. Regardless, this is a classic we’re happy to have. There are a few black and white illustrations throughout but not many.<br /><br />We watched the Disney movie after reading the book and I was surprised with the differences which included a switch up with the ending. There definitely wasn’t as much death and there were some scenes removed altogether. We loved the movie and actually liked the ending in the movie a little better.<br />I was excited to see that there’s a second book titled <i>Savage Sam</i>. We’ll be reading that one next.<br /><br />5*****<br /><br />This book is featured on Shabby Sunday @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2019/02/03/shabby-sunday-old-yeller-by-fred-gibson-1956-shabbysunday-bookreview-vintagebooks/">https://readrantrockandroll.com/2019/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14993667037744455993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15821046315838244491">I can only conclude that there must be something terribly wrong with me, that I would embark on a third reading of <i>Old Yeller</i>.<br/><br/>It's madness. It's the only explanation.<br/><br/>I just felt as though my 10-year-old was ready. And she was. I guess I felt ready again, too.<br/><br/>So we took on this 117 page classic from 1956, together, even though it had broken my heart twice before.<br/><br/>I was wondering if this daughter would consider the language dated, but, no, she took it all in stride. She was surprisingly unfazed tha</span>
  <span id="freeText15821046315838244491" style="display:none">I can only conclude that there must be something terribly wrong with me, that I would embark on a third reading of <i>Old Yeller</i>.<br /><br />It's madness. It's the only explanation.<br /><br />I just felt as though my 10-year-old was ready. And she was. I guess I felt ready again, too.<br /><br />So we took on this 117 page classic from 1956, together, even though it had broken my heart twice before.<br /><br />I was wondering if this daughter would consider the language dated, but, no, she took it all in stride. She was surprisingly unfazed that Pa had once had to kill a Comanche, Ma had to skin a deer, and Travis had to shoot several small animals. It was life in the 1800s, in the wild frontier that was Texas, and times weren't what they are now. <br /><br />And, yet, when we got to the first of the two pivotal parts of the heart-breaking plot, she jumped up and shouted, “WHY ARE YOU MAKING ME LISTEN TO THIS?”<br /><br />I asked her, “Would you like me to stop?”<br /><br />She sat back down and answered, “No.”<br /><br />When we got to the second sad part of the story, I collapsed in deep sobs, but I still heard her little voice say, “Mom, it's like <i>Charlotte's Web</i> all over again. Do you want me to read?”<br /><br />I pulled myself together and we finished the last part, the part that's so soul crushing, you almost can't get through it. But, like life, you prevail.<br /><br />In the end, we were holding each other by the forearms, foreheads pressed together, shaking and sobbing. When we stopped crying, I asked her, “Do you wish I hadn't read it to you?<br /><br />She paused, then answered, “Yes. No. I don't know.”<br /><br />I worried I'd made a bad decision as a mother. Asked her, “How many stars would you give it?”<br /><br />She looked up at me like I was an idiot and said, “Five stars. OBVIOUSLY.”<br /><br /><i>“Now the thing to do,” [Papa] went on, “is to try to forget it and go on being a man.”<br />“How?” I asked. “How can you forget a thing like that?”<br /><br />He studied me for a moment, then shook his head. “I guess I don't quite mean that,” he said. “It's not a thing you can forget. What I mean is, things like that happen. They may seem mighty cruel and unfair, but that's how life is part of the time. But that isn't the only way life is. A part of the time, it's mighty good. And a man can't afford to waste all the good part, worrying about the bad parts. That makes it all bad. . . You understand?”</i></span>

<div id="review_710123400" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/710123400" />
    <a title="Brian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1938805-brian"><img alt="Brian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442608867p2/1938805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/710123400?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian" href="/user/show/1938805-brian">Brian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/17187661-old-yeller">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Brian by: </span>
      Lynne King
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer710123400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12781579324542118457">This 1950s Pocket edition, purchased from a Sonoma used book store, presented today as a gift to my eight year old daughter (more on this later). After thanking me she asked me what it was about. I told her it's about a boy and his dog. She asked me if the dog dies. I told her he does, but that it is still a good book. She asked if I had read it. I told her I hadn't - only seen the movie. She asked me to read it for her first to make sure it wasn't too sad. She's on to me...<br/><br/>Our 14 year-old prota</span>
  <span id="freeText12781579324542118457" style="display:none">This 1950s Pocket edition, purchased from a Sonoma used book store, presented today as a gift to my eight year old daughter (more on this later). After thanking me she asked me what it was about. I told her it's about a boy and his dog. She asked me if the dog dies. I told her he does, but that it is still a good book. She asked if I had read it. I told her I hadn't - only seen the movie. She asked me to read it for her first to make sure it wasn't too sad. She's on to me...<br /><br />Our 14 year-old protagonist Travis comes of age when his father leaves him to be the man of the house while he does a cattle drive from Texas to Kansas. Gipson's frontiersy narrative and dialogue feels right, sounds right, for a book written for children in the 1950s about life in West Texas in the late 1860s. My memories of the movie are hazy, but it seems that the film action follows closely to the written word action, and while there is definitely sadness in the passing of Old Yeller, it doesn't feel like maudlin melancholy. As an eight year old it is the kind of book I would want to read about such weighty subjects as death, grieving, living. When I finished reading it, I handed the novel to my daughter and said, "It's not so sad. You'll like it." She's read the entire Laura Ingalls Wilder series. This book is a layup.<br /><br />When traveling my daughter often sees me reading on a Kindle or an iPad. She knows I am reading a book - she also knows that I prefer to read a physical copy rather than an E but that our luggage can only accommodate so many books (here in Florida I've been walking around with <i>Women and Men</i> like a KJV Bible clutched heavily to my chest). She asks when she will be able to read a book on the iPad; I know that in her lifetime a library will be as much of an anachronism as if I had a shelf of VHS tapes - but I want to hold out for as long as I can and help her to experience the tactile enjoyment of the tree book over the ebook. This paperback copy of Old Yeller is 60 years old, in decent shape and is only just showing the ravages of time with yellowing paper and crackling spine glue. While reading the book I hand it to my daughter and ask her to flip the pages under her nose and breath in. She does so, smiles. "You'll never get that from an ebook", I tell her. I hope she remembers this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12781579324542118457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_673175013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/673175013" />
    <a title="Lynne King" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15736557-lynne-king"><img alt="Lynne King" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357126217p2/15736557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/673175013?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynne King" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynne King" href="/user/show/15736557-lynne-king">Lynne King</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15736557-lynne-king?shelf=dogs">dogs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15736557-lynne-king?shelf=definitely-to-read">definitely-to-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer673175013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7059212168666748792">“Now Travis,’ he said, “you’re getting to be a big boy, and while I’m gone, you’ll be the man of the family. I want you to act like one. You take care of mama and Little Arliss. You look after the work and don’t wait around for your mama to point out what needs to be done. Think you can do that?”<br/><br/>“Yessir,” I said.<br/><br/>His father had to go away to get some “cash money” by selling his steer. But the boy wanted a horse. The upshot being that if he acted as a man when his father was away, he would be rewa</span>
  <span id="freeText7059212168666748792" style="display:none">“Now Travis,’ he said, “you’re getting to be a big boy, and while I’m gone, you’ll be the man of the family. I want you to act like one. You take care of mama and Little Arliss. You look after the work and don’t wait around for your mama to point out what needs to be done. Think you can do that?”<br /><br />“Yessir,” I said.<br /><br />His father had to go away to get some “cash money” by selling his steer. But the boy wanted a horse. The upshot being that if he acted as a man when his father was away, he would be rewarded with his wish upon his father’s return.<br /><br />And on that note his father left with the other steer herders and they went off to the cattle market in Kansas to return in the fall.<br /><br />I acquired this book on another whim. I wanted something “light” to read and I read an excellent review by Jim on Goodreads, so decided this was the book for me and a quick, light read too. How surprised I was when I started reading it and found out what a gem, well in fact it’s more of a gem, it’s a diamond and I absolutely loved it!<br /><br />Here we are in Texas in the late 1860s, to find the settlers who indeed had their work cut out for them in order to survive and bring up their families. I’m terrified of snakes here in France but to think of the wide selection of animals that could be found there on an everyday basis: bobcats, bears, wolves, panthers, rattlers, hogs, coons, etc. plus the odd raiding Indians. I’m not at all surprised that the settlers would naturally have dogs as guard dogs if nothing else. I believe that I would have either stayed indoors all the time, playing the helpless female or look for a good man who wanted to settle in safer climes. But still in the 1860s, I would imagine that a woman’s lot was a hard one and she had very little choice in life; certainly nothing like the 21st century career women with choices galore if they want to take advantage of it.<br /><br />The more I read about fourteen year old Travis’ family, mama and papa, of course, and five year-old Arliss (known as Little Arliss and what a terror he was, constantly causing problems), the more I became engrossed in this exciting, poignant, adventurous and yet magical book. There was the constant thrill of their life be it with an element of death living around the corner, living in a log cabin that the parents had built in a place that they named Birdsong Creek<br /><br />When Travis loses his beloved dog Bell in a rather nasty way, he swears he’ll never have another one, even though his father said that it essential for the safety of their daily lives. I know how he felt. When I lost my five year old black Labrador Jasper to a dreadful end, I also swore, no, I’ll never, ever have another dog. That emotional pain and the memories I would never consider again. I can equate this to childbirth. My mother told my father after the birth of my elder brother, no more children, one’s enough but still she went on to have three more children. So Travis although not wanting another dog, unsuspectingly does end up with one, and serendipitously too when one morning he finds Little Arliss playing with this ugly dog in their drinking water. Travis is furious and remembers his father telling him, when he loses Bell, to get another dog and Travis is adamant in that he won’t have it. Nevertheless, his mother is clever, for when his father is away at the cattle market, 600 miles away, with Travis ostensibly in charge (albeit under her watchful eye), she persuades him to let Little Arliss have the dog for company as he will be alone so much as she and Travis will be too busy to play with him. So Travis begrudgingly agrees and slowly begins to love Old Yeller and what a blessing this dog turned out to be. I actually had a lump in my throat from time to time as I continued reading this book.<br /><br />“We called him Old Yeller. The name had a sort of double meaning. One part meant that his short hair was a dingy yellow, a color that we called “yeller” in those days. The other meant that when he opened his head (a strange turn of phase); the sound he let out came closer to being a yell than a bark.”<br /><br />We live through the “trials and tribulations” of the family and Old Yeller surviving involvements with bears and hogs, and some of those sections were quite gruesome.<br /><br />I was amused when I saw that the family ate squirrel because they used to do that here about fifty years ago. I live here in France in “rusticana”, about forty miles from a city and this is a land of hunters and fishermen, so I could truly relate to this book.<br /><br />Also the medicinal aspects were interesting, for example, in that when the mother used poultices for wounds she prepared “mashed-up prickly-pear root to draw out the poison” and also horse’s hair for stitching up wounds as it was ostensibly the best.<br /><br />Lisbeth, who came to help out the family latterly when Travis gets involved in an accident, is a strange girl but she turns out well in the end and as for Old Yeller, what a fabulous find he turned out to be; saving the family on various occasions from some possibly very unfortunate outcomes. I could just continue in this vein. The truly sad part is when hydrophobia (rabies I guess) strikes and does the family suffer in that regard.<br /><br />I initially thought that Old Yeller was the catalyst in this book but it is indeed the horse as Travis, through sheer hard work, progresses through the early stages of manhood. The horse will be his ultimate reward when he has proved himself to be a man. The ultimate test for this incredible young man and was I impressed.<br /><br />This is an excellent read for all ages. I have the Kindle version and I’m now going to order a hardback copy so that I can browse through it, as will be my want from time to time.<br /><br />This is an absolutely super read and my only regret is that I would have loved to have read it as a child.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7059212168666748792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer82508770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10407221171535098819">Let me say first that some love this book and to be fair I never read it except to get an idea of the story. You will find in my books low ratings for Black Beauty, The Yearling, Old Yeller and any books that have the "pain of life motif" in common. By the way this includes Cold Mountain. Look up my review and you'll see I try to give recognition that it's well written but just not a book I can like. And these ratings are how I feel and what I think of these books. Some will say how they love th</span>
  <span id="freeText10407221171535098819" style="display:none">Let me say first that some love this book and to be fair I never read it except to get an idea of the story. You will find in my books low ratings for Black Beauty, The Yearling, Old Yeller and any books that have the "pain of life motif" in common. By the way this includes Cold Mountain. Look up my review and you'll see I try to give recognition that it's well written but just not a book I can like. And these ratings are how I feel and what I think of these books. Some will say how they love these books and how possibly there was just no other way to "realistically" end the story. <br /><br />I grew up in the Smokies and without going over my childhood, I had 2 dogs killed...shot. I've lived through the loss of beloved animals, beloved people and beloved relationships...I don't need a novel that leads me through "what pain is". If a book is of the "life is tough and then you die school", it's going to get a "down check" from me. While fiction does instruct, there are some lessons I learned from life, I don't need to have them rehashed in leisure time activities.<br /><br />This book/movie (I know but in this case I'll lump them together) scarred me and I suspect other young people. Ask anyone who has loved a dog (an animal) if the fact that you get a "new puppy" after you had to kill the dog makes up for it. Maybe this book is well written. I sometimes suspect that many if not most of the people who come to "love" books like this maybe haven't gone through that pain in life. If you have and you still love this work, well, good. I can not say that.</span>

<div id="review_574121761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/574121761" />
    <a title="Jackson Burnett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10106571-jackson-burnett"><img alt="Jackson Burnett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455878630p2/10106571.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/574121761?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackson Burnett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackson Burnett" href="/user/show/10106571-jackson-burnett">Jackson Burnett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10106571-jackson-burnett?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10106571-jackson-burnett?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10106571-jackson-burnett?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10106571-jackson-burnett?shelf=western">western</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer574121761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6418512578846603608">This review is for mothers and fathers of sons written by a man with no children. Forgive my presumptuousness, but please don't let my lack of experience stop you from reading. <br/><br/>Here's the story of Old Yeller: Daddy, Mama, young son, and early teenage son live as a family on the Texas frontier. To provide for the family, Daddy has to go on a cattle drive to Kansas. Before he leaves, Daddy takes the oldest son aside and tells him he is going to have to be the man of the house since Daddy will be g</span>
  <span id="freeText6418512578846603608" style="display:none">This review is for mothers and fathers of sons written by a man with no children. Forgive my presumptuousness, but please don't let my lack of experience stop you from reading. <br /><br />Here's the story of Old Yeller: Daddy, Mama, young son, and early teenage son live as a family on the Texas frontier. To provide for the family, Daddy has to go on a cattle drive to Kansas. Before he leaves, Daddy takes the oldest son aside and tells him he is going to have to be the man of the house since Daddy will be gone the next few months.<br /><br />When you get to this anachronistic charge, you may be tempted to throw the book down and dismiss the entire book as patriarchal and condescending. If you have sons, keep reading. You might even consider having your sons read this book. In truth, Old Yeller is the timeless story of the journey a boy goes through to become a man. <br /><br />I get tired of encountering men who don't know what it means to be a man, who don't speak the truth, who don't keep their word, who show no respect, who look for the easy way out, who show no backbone, and have few principles. In short, men who refuse to accept responsibility. I suspect these men have been shielded from hard and unpleasant tasks, and by being so protected, they fail to learn to do the right thing, regardless of its difficulty.<br /><br />I have seen Old Yeller on film two or three times and had read the book in years past multiple times. I thought I was ready. I really did.<br /><br />Last Sunday, I put my faithful dog to sleep.<br /><br />It was the right and merciful thing to do.<br /><br />It still broke my heart.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6418512578846603608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3012720574?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/61672374-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61672374-catherine?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3012720574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14445443929130587576"><i>What I mean is, things like that happen. They may seem mighty cruel and unfair, but that's how life is a part of the time. But that isn't the only way life is. A part of the time, it's mighty good. And a man can't afford to waste all the good parts worrying about the bad parts. That makes it all bad… you understand?</i><br/><br/>This book totally exceeded my expectations. My favourite thing about it was the narrative style - it really felt like I was sitting with the protagonist, Travis, while he was giving m</span>
  <span id="freeText14445443929130587576" style="display:none"><i>What I mean is, things like that happen. They may seem mighty cruel and unfair, but that's how life is a part of the time. But that isn't the only way life is. A part of the time, it's mighty good. And a man can't afford to waste all the good parts worrying about the bad parts. That makes it all bad… you understand?</i><br /><br />This book totally exceeded my expectations. My favourite thing about it was the narrative style - it really felt like I was sitting with the protagonist, Travis, while he was giving me a first hand account of what life was like with Old Yeller. I also laughed out loud at certain parts (mainly the ones having to do with Travis's five year old brother Arlis) and admittedly shed a tear at the end. It was really nice to see Travis progressively take such a liking to Old Yeller after initially being so averse to the whole idea of taking him in as their family's dog.<br /><br />This is such a heartwarming story, and if you're into books about animals, you definitely need to read this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14445443929130587576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_183265301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183265301" />
    <a title="Book Concierge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge"><img alt="Book Concierge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324904606p2/1628041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183265301?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Book Concierge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Book Concierge" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge">Book Concierge</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=dogs">dogs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=texas">texas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=19th-century">19th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=nature">nature</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183265301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9207340244993115011">Gipson’s simply told tale of a boy and his dog living in the Texas Hill Country of 1860 is a genuine classic of children’s literature. Travis Coates is only 14 years old, but while his father is off for months on a cattle drive, he is the “man of the house,” left on the homestead with his mother and younger brother, 5-year-old Arliss. A stray yellow mutt of a dog, with one ear virtually chewed off, and only a stump of a tail, shows up one day. He’s a no good, thieving rascal – taking their meat </span>
  <span id="freeText9207340244993115011" style="display:none">Gipson’s simply told tale of a boy and his dog living in the Texas Hill Country of 1860 is a genuine classic of children’s literature. Travis Coates is only 14 years old, but while his father is off for months on a cattle drive, he is the “man of the house,” left on the homestead with his mother and younger brother, 5-year-old Arliss. A stray yellow mutt of a dog, with one ear virtually chewed off, and only a stump of a tail, shows up one day. He’s a no good, thieving rascal – taking their meat and stealing eggs when he can – but he proves himself to be a key defender of the family when he faces a bear that is targeting Arliss. Just as Old Yeller worms his way into the family’s hearts, this book will burrow into the reader’s heart. <br /><br />I am not a “dog person,” but I really connected with this book. I think this in part due to the fact that I grew up in the Texas Hill Country, so the scenery was alive in my imagination. But more importantly, I connected to the way Gipson portrayed the characters’ emotions – fear, love, irritation, loyalty, happiness, sorrow. <br /><br />This little book packs a big wallop. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9207340244993115011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Too many years & too mixed up from seeing the movie, which changes some things.   <span id="freeText16935432192046523429" style="display:none">I'm so glad I listened to this again. Fantastic narrator, perfect voice for the part.<br /><br />I thought I remembered the book well, but I hadn't, not really. Too many years &amp; too mixed up from seeing the movie, which changes some things. Super movie, but nothing beats the book.<br /><br />Gipson perfectly captured a mature 14 year old, the kind of boy I'd expect given the times, post Civil War Texas, late 1860's. He wasn't always perfect, but that just made him more real. The feelings he had were very well done as were the descriptions of life at the time. What a hard life they had. Makes me glad to live now.<br /><br />I won't even bother saying anything about that old yeller dog. Everyone knows. I will say the book handles the end better than the movie, IMO. Yes, it's sad, but so realistic &amp; fantastic in its own way.<br /><br />If you haven't read this in sometime, I can't recommend a reread highly enough. This audio book was from my local library, so easy to get, quick, &amp; free. There's no excuse not to.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8240453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12815799829074418304">This is the first book that ever made me cry. I would read it during my study period in the 4th grade each day for almost 2 weeks (it was my class copy-- so I had to keep putting it back and hoping no one else would take it). I held my tears back until the lunch bell rang and then ran for the bathroom to cry. It may have been the first time I realized how incredible it was to read.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8879939079158670286">One more children's classic that I wish so much I had read as a child. I watched the movie many, many times as it was often played in the after-school special time slot. If you have seen the movie or read the book you will know that I sobbed each time -- and again when I finished the last words of the book.<br/><br/><b>Old Yeller</b> is the story of a 14 year old boy left to take care of his family when his father must leave for a long period of time for some work. Told by his father “you are the man of the fami</span>
  <span id="freeText8879939079158670286" style="display:none">One more children's classic that I wish so much I had read as a child. I watched the movie many, many times as it was often played in the after-school special time slot. If you have seen the movie or read the book you will know that I sobbed each time -- and again when I finished the last words of the book.<br /><br /><b>Old Yeller</b> is the story of a 14 year old boy left to take care of his family when his father must leave for a long period of time for some work. Told by his father “you are the man of the family now," Travis takes the comments seriously taking on a huge volume of physical work, hunt for food, help care for his little brother and more. Luckily for him he also comes to love an old, beat-up mutt he calls Old Yeller. And that dog proves himself worthy of the love.<br /><br />But life can be cruel and unfair and for this boy it is extremely hard. Old Yeller gets rabies and Travis must shoot the dog to protect his family. (No spoiler as it is revealed on the first page.) The book is sweet, vivid, emotional and humbling. It is beautiful and heart-warming, as well as difficult and wrenching.</span>

<div id="review_42423167" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42423167" />
    <a title="Jey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1386477-jey"><img alt="Jey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217564809p2/1386477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42423167?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jey" href="/user/show/1386477-jey">Jey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1386477-jey?shelf=books-for-young-people">books-for-young-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1386477-jey?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer42423167&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42423167" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6157086874454816031">As the inagural book for the Georgics class that I'm taking from LEMI this semester, Old Yeller was perfect. This book covered so many of the topics and themes of Georgics, I was surprised. <br/><br/>This book talked a lot about the cycle of birth/death. This cycle is almost foreign to us anymore, and I believe that that isn't a good thing. Because death is such a mysterious thing, it tends to be shocking for us, and I'm quite certain that God never intended it to be so. One of my favorite quotes from the</span>
  <span id="freeText6157086874454816031" style="display:none">As the inagural book for the Georgics class that I'm taking from LEMI this semester, Old Yeller was perfect. This book covered so many of the topics and themes of Georgics, I was surprised. <br /><br />This book talked a lot about the cycle of birth/death. This cycle is almost foreign to us anymore, and I believe that that isn't a good thing. Because death is such a mysterious thing, it tends to be shocking for us, and I'm quite certain that God never intended it to be so. One of my favorite quotes from the book is when Travis is talking with his dad about his feelings after Yeller's death. His dad says, "Now the thing to do,"he went on, "is to try to forget it and go on being a man."<br />"How?" I asked. "How can you forget a thing like that?"<br />He studied me for a moment, then shook his head. "I guess I don't quite mean that," he said. "It's not a thing you can forget. I don't guess it's a thing that you ought to forget. What I mean is, things like that happen. They may seem might cruel and unfair, but that's how life is a part of the time. But that isn't the only way life is. A part of the time, it's mighty good. And a man can't afford to waste all the good part, worrying about the bad parts. That makes it all bad."<br /><br />Another point made in the book that I really liked was about man's dependence on the land. This is something I think we have totally lost in our society, for sure to our detriment. Two quotes I liked about this were when the father was leaving. He said to his son, "Now, there're the cows to milk and wood to cut and young pigs to mark and fresh meat to shoot. But mainly there's the corn patch. If you don't work it right or if you let the varmints eat up the roasting ears, we'll be without bread corn for the winter." After the father left, Travis says, "Now it was home, too. And while Papa was gone it was up to me to look after it." How many of us understand how important that really is?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6157086874454816031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Bob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4814165-bob"><img alt="Bob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295123458p2/4814165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3124579074?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob" href="/user/show/4814165-bob">Bob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/16039375-old-yeller">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4814165-bob?shelf=fiction-general">fiction-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4814165-bob?shelf=20th-century-classics">20th-century-classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4814165-bob?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3124579074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11955299709551446657">I am amazed at number of books I haven't read that I should have read when I was young. This is certainly one of them, I am in my sixties and I’ve just now read this wonderful story. <br/> <br/>This is a story about a boy growing up, and becoming a man at the early age of fourteen. <br/><br/>When Travis’s father must leave the family on important business, Travis must step up and take care of his family. His father tells him that he must be responsible for the family’s wellbeing. This “you are the man of the family</span>
  <span id="freeText11955299709551446657" style="display:none">I am amazed at number of books I haven't read that I should have read when I was young. This is certainly one of them, I am in my sixties and I’ve just now read this wonderful story. <br /> <br />This is a story about a boy growing up, and becoming a man at the early age of fourteen. <br /><br />When Travis’s father must leave the family on important business, Travis must step up and take care of his family. His father tells him that he must be responsible for the family’s wellbeing. This “you are the man of the family now” speech is not just a platitude so that Travis will be well behaved for his mother. Much of his family’s short and long term survival now does indeed rest on his shoulders.<br /><br />The work is long in hours and physically demanding and Travis is proves up to the tasks. In addition to the hard work Travis is learning the maturity required of a man. He learns to be more patient with his young brother, even when he feels that switching him is a better choice than coaxing him to behave. As Travis grows stronger physically and mentally he is faced with the most difficult decision a person can face. He must make the life and death decision about something loved. <br /><br />Travis is forced to kill his beloved dog Old Yeller, that’s not a spoiler it’s stated on page one. Again, Travis understands his responsibility, and knows the danger Old Yeller has now become to his mother and brother. He does what is necessary, I know from my own similar experience at the age of sixteen how difficult and emotional a decision it was. Life can at times be cruel and hard. <br /><br />I wonder given the nature of this story and my perception of today’s world, will young parents feel this book is inappropriate for young children. Do young people today feel that the life lessons told in this book are too cruel and harsh for today’s youth? I hope not.<br /><br />This is an excellent story. I wish I had read it when I was a boy and this had been a reread. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11955299709551446657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/807797774" />
    <a title="Marcia Van Camp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1198638-marcia-van-camp"><img alt="Marcia Van Camp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252969172p2/1198638.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/807797774?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marcia Van Camp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marcia Van Camp" href="/user/show/1198638-marcia-van-camp">Marcia Van Camp</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer807797774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8752016784111872418">My mother read to us constantly when we were young, and still enjoys reading to us as adults. When I was about 9 years old, we decided to read Old Yeller together. I cannot remember why we chose the book, but I believe it was new to both of us. It was a special time for me, as I had my mom all to myself in a busy house, and we both really enjoyed the story, characters, and the writing. I remember the ending, and I won't spoil it for those who may not be familiar with the tale. What I will say, i</span>
  <span id="freeText8752016784111872418" style="display:none">My mother read to us constantly when we were young, and still enjoys reading to us as adults. When I was about 9 years old, we decided to read Old Yeller together. I cannot remember why we chose the book, but I believe it was new to both of us. It was a special time for me, as I had my mom all to myself in a busy house, and we both really enjoyed the story, characters, and the writing. I remember the ending, and I won't spoil it for those who may not be familiar with the tale. What I will say, is that Old Yeller, was the first book that taught me as a youth, in a deep and powerful way, how strong the written word can be. I remember being almost shocked that I could feel such immense empathy for characters who I knew logically were not real. Even after all these years, I still have very strong feelings about this book. I will always love this book, and I hope many others will love it as well.<br /><br />I came across this quote recently which when I read it, I immediately thought of Old Yeller.<br /><br />“Once, in my father’s bookshop, I heard a regular customer say that few things leave a deeper mark on a reader than the first book that finds its way into his heart. Those first images, the echo of words we think we have left behind, accompany us throughout our lives and sculpt a palace in our memory to which, sooner or later — no matter how many books we read, how many worlds we discover, or how much we learn or forget — we will return.” <br /><br />—Carlos Ruiz Zafón, The Shadow of the Wind</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7929797636163705911">What an excellent book. Although I am in my 50s I have never read this or seen the movie. I remember my grandmother telling me I was too "tender-hearted" for it. I finally read it after it laid on my shelf for literally decades. Old Yeller is a classic coming-of-age book where a teenage boy must take on adult responsibilities and as he learns, he matures. It also has all the bittersweet moments one would expect in a dog story. Another plus for this book is the almost diary-like aspect of day to </span>
  <span id="freeText7929797636163705911" style="display:none">What an excellent book. Although I am in my 50s I have never read this or seen the movie. I remember my grandmother telling me I was too "tender-hearted" for it. I finally read it after it laid on my shelf for literally decades. Old Yeller is a classic coming-of-age book where a teenage boy must take on adult responsibilities and as he learns, he matures. It also has all the bittersweet moments one would expect in a dog story. Another plus for this book is the almost diary-like aspect of day to day work on the frontier farm. I appreciated the lovely descriptive prose which struck the perfect balance of vivid imagery without clouding the narrative. It is well worth reading. The best thing for me is I have the sequel Savage Sam already on my shelf. Perhaps given enough time I can work up the strength to read it too. : )</span>

<div id="review_2966762840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2966762840" />
    <a title="John Turner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17408028-john-turner"><img alt="John Turner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475875543p2/17408028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2966762840?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Turner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Turner" href="/user/show/17408028-john-turner">John Turner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780395732595" href="/book/show/1444266.Old_Yeller">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17408028-john-turner?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2966762840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12733042630941994034">Over the last 60 years, I've read this book numerous times, so many times, I've lost track. Twice in the past two years, for sure. Every read is fresh and entertaining. It's a story about a boy and his dog, a book purposely written for the juvenile reader, but one adults can readily enjoy.<br/><br/>Travis hates the old, yellow cur when it first shows up on his family farm. As Travis narrates the story, they named him Old Yeller, first for his dirty yellow color, then for his penchant to howl, a yeller rat</span>
  <span id="freeText12733042630941994034" style="display:none">Over the last 60 years, I've read this book numerous times, so many times, I've lost track. Twice in the past two years, for sure. Every read is fresh and entertaining. It's a story about a boy and his dog, a book purposely written for the juvenile reader, but one adults can readily enjoy.<br /><br />Travis hates the old, yellow cur when it first shows up on his family farm. As Travis narrates the story, they named him Old Yeller, first for his dirty yellow color, then for his penchant to howl, a yeller rather than a barker. Travis' brother, Little Arliss, immediately claimed the dog and they became fast friends, falling all over each other as dogs and little boys are prone to do. But the dog grows on Travis and they share many adventures.<br /><br />Having read the book and seen the movie, I know the tragedy of the ending but, the writing is so tight and moving that I never fail to get a lump in my throat and a tear in my eye during the last 25 pages. <br /><br />Fred Gipson was born and died in Mason County, Texas, the same hill country where this story takes place. Like young Arliss, he spent a lot of time in the woods watching animals. He also spent a lot of "old timers," listening to their stories, where Gipson developed his love of "storytelling." He said that he especially enjoyed writing stories for young people because all they ask is that the author "write a simple and honest story." Old Yeller was an instant success when it was published, named a Newerry Honor book in 1957. It was made into a popular movie that same year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12733042630941994034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_269104129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269104129" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7356691-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325898058p2/7356691.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269104129?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/7356691-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269104129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14797837055936043990">I read this as a kid and really liked it, and I just re-read it with one of my students. <br/>It has lot of problems inherent in its time, like racism and mild sexism, but on the whole I think it stands up okay.<br/><br/>I think the important thing with books like these is that when grief is experienced (because it will be) there's an understanding that you're not alone. When Travis says he felt nothing but hurt for weeks, there's something there that can be recognized, and I think there's a kind of comfort in</span>
  <span id="freeText14797837055936043990" style="display:none">I read this as a kid and really liked it, and I just re-read it with one of my students. <br />It has lot of problems inherent in its time, like racism and mild sexism, but on the whole I think it stands up okay.<br /><br />I think the important thing with books like these is that when grief is experienced (because it will be) there's an understanding that you're not alone. When Travis says he felt nothing but hurt for weeks, there's something there that can be recognized, and I think there's a kind of comfort in that. The point of the book isn't "terrible things happen in life," the point is that pain doesn't have to be isolating. <br />There have been many times in my life when I have wondered if anyone has ever felt the way I do, and in those moments I have often been able to point to a novel and say, "this is how I feel." Not only does that tell me I'm not alone (someone was able to write these feelings down after all), but I can find others who relate to the book. Plus, it can help me communicate my emotions to people who might not otherwise understand. I want to say how important a tool that is for children, but I think it's an important tool for all of us. <br />I mention all this just because I often see people condemning grief-filled books, especially those that are meant for children, as being cruel way to teach what life is about, but I don't think that's fair. They have more to do with empathy, comfort, and communication than anything else. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14797837055936043990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo"><img alt="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448623481p2/3615945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242342561?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" href="/user/show/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo">Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060739454" href="/book/show/130582.Old_Yeller">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=summer-2014">summer-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=permanent-library">permanent-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=great-literary-fiction">great-literary-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242342561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11615975567529680188">I still love this book about a boy and a dog he never wanted after losing his faithful old dog, Bell. He wanted a horse. His father promised that he'd get one after he returned from selling some cattle in Kansas. All Travis had to do is take care of his mother and his little brother, Arliss. Farm chores were a given. Then comes a mangy, ratty dog who steals eggs and such from them. He sees Arliss with the mutt at the trough. His mother suggests that the little boy will need a companion to play w</span>
  <span id="freeText11615975567529680188" style="display:none">I still love this book about a boy and a dog he never wanted after losing his faithful old dog, Bell. He wanted a horse. His father promised that he'd get one after he returned from selling some cattle in Kansas. All Travis had to do is take care of his mother and his little brother, Arliss. Farm chores were a given. Then comes a mangy, ratty dog who steals eggs and such from them. He sees Arliss with the mutt at the trough. His mother suggests that the little boy will need a companion to play with, to keep Arliss company while she and Travis are working the farm. <br /> <br /><i>“We called him Old Yeller. The name had a sort of double meaning. One part meant that his short hair was a dingy yellow, a color that we called “yeller” in those days. The other meant that when he opened his head (a strange turn of phase); the sound he let out came closer to being a yell than a bark.</i><br /> <br />Old Yeller slowly becomes part of their lives and saves the family in many situations, but alas Travis cannot save his precious buddy; he is the one who had to shoot Old Yeller.<br /> <br />Gipson accurately describes 1860s Texas and weaves a great story about relationships, love, and loss. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11615975567529680188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TXOPELwVkvtsYrxcn3efZnJX2dC8QPYt1xmIzEOOgvMR7CA3FlFx56uShT/W6h8+4VkOy0VFQTKrII1EOrH2Iw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
